<DIV style="width: 90%; margin-left: 5%"><!-- BEGIN PAGE WIDTH -->
<!-- XBRL Pagebreak End -->

<DIV style="margin-top: 12pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; font-size: 14pt; font-family: Arial, Helvetica; color: #000000; background: transparent">

    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">SPDR

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <B><FONT style="font-size: 14pt">Notes to Financial
    Statements</FONT></B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">

<DIV style="font-size: 11pt; margin-left: 0%; width: 99%;  align: left; border-bottom: 1pt solid #000000"></DIV>



<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: Arial, Helvetica; color: #000000; background: transparent">

    <TD width="92%"></TD>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD>
    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">Note&#160;1&#160;&#151;
    </FONT></B>
</TD>
    <TD>
    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">Organization</FONT></B>
</TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>



<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    SPDR S&#038;P 500 ETF Trust (the &#147;Trust&#148;), formerly
    the SPDR Trust, Series&#160;1, is a unit investment trust
    created under the laws of the State of New York and registered
    under the Investment Company Act of 1940, as amended. The Trust
    was created to provide investors with the opportunity to
    purchase a security representing a proportionate undivided
    interest in a portfolio of securities consisting of
    substantially all of the component common stocks, in
    substantially the same weighting, which comprise the
    Standard&#160;&#038; Poor&#146;s 500 Composite Price Index (the
    &#147;S&#038;P 500 Index&#148;). Each unit of fractional
    undivided interest in the Trust is referred to as a
    &#147;Unit&#148;. The Trust commenced operations on
    January&#160;22, 1993 upon the initial issuance of 150,000 Units
    (equivalent to three &#147;Creation Units&#148;&#160;&#151; see
    Note&#160;4)&#160;in exchange for a portfolio of securities
    assembled to reflect the intended portfolio composition of the
    Trust.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    Under the Amended and Restated Standard Terms and Conditions of
    the Trust, as amended (&#147;Trust&#160;Agreement&#148;), PDR
    Services, LLC, as Sponsor of the Trust (&#147;Sponsor&#148;),
    and State Street Bank and Trust&#160;Company, as Trustee of the
    Trust (&#147;Trustee&#148;), are indemnified against certain
    liabilities arising out of the performance of their duties to
    the Trust. Additionally, in the normal course of business, the
    Trust enters into contracts that contain general indemnification
    clauses. The Trust&#146;s maximum exposure under these
    arrangements is unknown as this would involve future claims that
    may be made against the Trust that have not yet occurred.
    However, based on experience, the Trust expects the risk of
    material loss to be remote.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    On February 15, 2011, NYSE Euronext (the parent of the Sponsor)
    and Deutsche Boerse AG announced that they have entered into a
    business combination agreement subject to approval by their
    shareholders as well as approval by the relevant regulatory
    authorities in the U.S. and Europe, and other closing conditions.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: Arial, Helvetica; color: #000000; background: transparent">

    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">Note&#160;2&#160;&#151;
    </FONT></B>

    <TD>
    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">Significant
    Accounting Policies</FONT></B>
</TD>
</TR>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    The following is a summary of significant accounting policies
    followed by the Trust in the preparation of its financial
    statements:
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    The preparation of financial statements in accordance with U.S.
    generally accepted accounting principles requires management to
    make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts
    and disclosures in the financial statements. Actual results
    could differ from those estimates.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: Arial, Helvetica; color: #000000; background: transparent">

    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">Security
    Valuation</FONT></B>
</DIV>



<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    The value of the Trust&#146;s portfolio securities is based on
    the market price of the securities, which generally means a
    valuation obtained from an exchange or other market (or based on
    a price quotation or other equivalent indication of value
    supplied by an exchange or other market) or a valuation obtained
    from an independent pricing service. If a security&#146;s market
    price is not readily available or does not otherwise accurately
    reflect the fair value of the security, the security will be
    valued by another method that the Trustee believes will better
    reflect fair value in accordance with the Trust&#146;s valuation
    policies and procedures. The Trustee has established a Pricing
    and Investment Committee (the &#147;Committee&#148;) for the
    purpose of valuing securities for which market quotations are
    not readily available or do not otherwise accurately reflect the
    fair value of the security. The Committee, subject to oversight
    by the Trustee, may use fair value pricing in a variety of
    circumstances, including but not limited to, situations when
    trading in a security has been suspended or halted. Accordingly,
    the Trust&#146;s net asset value may reflect certain portfolio
    securities&#146; fair values rather than their market prices.
    Fair value pricing involves subjective judgments and it is
    possible that the fair value determination for a security is
    materially different than the value that could be received on
    the sale of the security.
</DIV>
<!-- XBRL Pagebreak Begin -->

<P align="center" style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <BR>

<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="width: 90%; margin-left: 5%"><!-- BEGIN PAGE WIDTH -->

<DIV style="margin-top: 12pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; font-size: 14pt; font-family: Arial, Helvetica; color: #000000; background: transparent">

    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">SPDR
    S&#038;P 500 ETF Trust</FONT></B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <B><FONT style="font-size: 14pt">Notes to Financial Statements
    (continued)</FONT></B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <B><FONT style="font-size: 12pt">March&#160;31, 2011
    (Unaudited)</FONT></B>
</DIV>

<DIV style="font-size: 11pt; margin-left: 0%; width: 100%;  align: left; border-bottom: 1pt solid #000000"></DIV>
<DIV style="margin-top: 5pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: Arial, Helvetica; color: #000000; background: transparent">


</DIV>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: Arial, Helvetica; color: #000000; background: transparent">

<TR>
    <TD width="8%"></TD>
    <TD width="92%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD>
    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">Note&#160;2&#160;&#151;
    </FONT></B>
</TD>
    <TD>
    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">Significant
    Accounting Policies&#160;&#150;&#160;(continued)</FONT></B>
</TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>
<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>
<!-- XBRL Pagebreak End -->

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    The Trust continues to follow the authoritative guidance for
    fair value measurements and the fair value option for financial
    assets and financial liabilities. The guidance for the fair
    value option for financial assets and financial liabilities
    provides the Trust the irrevocable option to measure many
    financial assets and liabilities at fair value with changes in
    fair value recognized in earnings. The guidance also establishes
    a hierarchy for inputs used in measuring fair value that
    maximizes the use of observable inputs and minimizes the use of
    unobservable inputs by requiring that the most observable inputs
    be used when available. The guidance establishes three levels of
    inputs that may be used to measure fair value:
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

<TR>
    <TD width="1%"></TD>
    <TD width="99%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top" style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD>    &#149;&#160;
</TD>
    <TD align="left">    Level&#160;1&#160;&#151;&#160;quoted prices in active markets
    for identical investments
</TD>
</TR>


<TR style="line-height: 6pt; font-size: 1pt"><TD>&nbsp;</TD></TR>


<TR valign="top" style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD>    &#149;&#160;
</TD>
    <TD align="left">    Level&#160;2&#160;&#151;&#160;other significant observable
    inputs (including, but not limited to, quoted prices for similar
    investments, interest rates, prepayment speeds, credit risk,
    etc.)
</TD>
</TR>


<TR style="line-height: 6pt; font-size: 1pt"><TD>&nbsp;</TD></TR>


<TR valign="top" style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD>    &#149;&#160;
</TD>
    <TD align="left">    Level&#160;3&#160;&#151;&#160;significant unobservable inputs
    (including the Trust&#146;s own assumptions in determining the
    fair value of investments)
</TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    Investments that use Level&#160;2 or Level&#160;3 inputs may
    include, but are not limited to: (i)&#160;an unlisted security
    related to corporate actions; (ii)&#160;a restricted security
    (e.g., one that may not be publicly sold without registration
    under the Securities Act of 1933, as amended); (iii)&#160;a
    security whose trading has been suspended or which has been
    de-listed from its primary trading exchange; (iv)&#160;a
    security that is thinly traded; (v)&#160;a security in default
    or bankruptcy proceedings for which there is no current market
    quotation; (vi)&#160;a security affected by currency controls or
    restrictions; and (vii)&#160;a security affected by a
    significant event (e.g., an event that occurs after the close of
    the markets on which the security is traded but before the time
    as of which the Trust&#146;s net assets are computed and that
    may materially affect the value of the Trust&#146;s
    investments). Examples of events that may be &#147;significant
    events&#148; are government actions, natural disasters, armed
    conflicts, acts of terrorism, and significant market
    fluctuations.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    Fair value pricing could result in a difference between the
    prices used to calculate the Trust&#146;s net asset value and
    the prices used by the S&#038;P 500 Index, which, in turn, could
    result in a difference between the Trust&#146;s performance and
    the performance of the S&#038;P 500 Index. The inputs or
    methodology used for valuation are not necessarily an indication
    of the risk associated with investing in those investments. The
    type of inputs used to value each security is identified in the
    Schedule of Investments, which also includes a breakdown of the
    Trust&#146;s investment by industry.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: Arial, Helvetica; color: #000000; background: transparent">

    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">Subsequent
    Events</FONT></B>
</DIV>



<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    Management has determined that there are no subsequent events or
    transactions that would have materially impacted the
    Trust&#146;s financial statements as presented.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: Arial, Helvetica; color: #000000; background: transparent">

    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">Investment
    Risk</FONT></B>
</DIV>



<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    The Trust&#146;s investments are exposed to risks, such as
    market risk. Due to the level of risk associated with certain
    investments it is at least reasonably possible that changes in
    the values of investment securities will occur in the near term
    and that such changes could materially affect the amounts
    reported in the financial statements.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    An investment in the Trust involves risks similar to those of
    investing in any fund of equity securities, such as market
    fluctuations caused by such factors as economic and political
    developments, changes in interest rates and perceived trends in
    stock prices. The value of a Unit will decline, more or less, in
    correlation with any decline in value of the S&#038;P 500 Index.
    The values of equity securities could decline generally or could
    underperform other investments. The Trust would not sell
</DIV>
<!-- XBRL Paragraph Pagebreak -->

    S&#038;P 500 ETF Trust</FONT></B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <B><FONT style="font-size: 14pt">Notes to Financial Statements
    (continued)</FONT></B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <B><FONT style="font-size: 12pt">March&#160;31, 2011

</DIV>

<DIV style="font-size: 11pt; margin-left: 0%; width: 100%;  align: left; border-bottom: 1pt solid #000000"></DIV>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD>
    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">Note&#160;2&#160;&#151;
    </FONT></B>
</TD>
    <TD>
    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">Significant
    Accounting Policies&#160;&#150;&#160;(continued)</FONT></B>
</TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>
<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>
<!-- XBRL Pagebreak End -->

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    an equity security because the security&#146;s issuer was in
    financial trouble unless that security is removed from the
    S&#038;P 500 Index.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: Arial, Helvetica; color: #000000; background: transparent">

    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">Investment
    Transactions</FONT></B>
</DIV>



<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    Investment transactions are recorded on the trade date. Realized
    gains and losses from the sale or disposition of securities are
    recorded on the identified cost basis. Dividend income is
    recorded on the ex-dividend date.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: Arial, Helvetica; color: #000000; background: transparent">

    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">Distributions
    to Unitholders</FONT></B>
</DIV>



<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    The Trust declares and distributes dividends from net investment
    income to its unitholders quarterly. The Trust declares and
    distributes net realized capital gains, if any, at least
    annually.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    Broker-dealers, at their own discretion, may offer a dividend
    reinvestment service under which additional Units may be
    purchased in the secondary market at current market prices.
    Investors should consult their broker-dealer for further
    information regarding any dividend reinvestment service offered
    by such broker-dealer.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: Arial, Helvetica; color: #000000; background: transparent">

    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">Equalization</FONT></B>
</DIV>



<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    The Trust follows the accounting practice known as
    &#147;Equalization&#148; by which a portion of the proceeds from
    sales and costs of reacquiring the Trust&#146;s Units,
    equivalent on a per Unit basis to the amount of distributable
    net investment income on the date of the transaction, is
    credited or charged to undistributed net investment income. As a
    result, undistributed net investment income per Unit is
    unaffected by sales or reacquisitions of the Trust&#146;s Units.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: Arial, Helvetica; color: #000000; background: transparent">

    <B><FONT style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times">U.S.
    Federal Income Tax</FONT></B>
</DIV>



<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    For U.S. federal income tax purposes, the Trust has qualified as
    a &#147;regulated investment company&#148; under Subchapter M of
    the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended (a
    &#147;RIC&#148;) and intends to continue to qualify as a RIC. As
    a RIC, the Trust will generally not be subject to
    U.S.&#160;federal income tax for any taxable year on income,
    including net capital gains, that it distributes to the holders
    of Units, provided that it distributes on a timely basis at
    least 90% of its &#147;investment company taxable income&#148;
    (generally, its taxable income other than net capital gain) for
    such taxable year. In addition, provided that the Trust
    distributes during each calendar year substantially all of its
    ordinary income and capital gains, the Trust will not be subject
    to U.S.&#160;federal excise tax.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    The Trust has reviewed the tax positions for the open tax years
    as of September&#160;30, 2010 and has determined that no
    provision for income tax is required in the Trust&#146;s
    financial statements. The Trust&#146;s federal tax returns for
    the prior three fiscal years remain subject to examination by
    the Trust&#146;s major tax jurisdictions, which include the
    United States of America and the State of New York.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    During the six months ended March&#160;31, 2011, the Trust
    reclassified $8,434,336,807 of non-taxable net security gains
    realized from the in-kind redemption of Creation Units
    (Note&#160;4)&#160;as an increase to paid in capital in the
    Statement of Assets and Liabilities. At March&#160;31, 2011, the
    cost of investments for federal income tax purposes was
    substantially the same as the cost for financial reporting
    purposes. Accordingly, the cost was $87,353,562,440, gross
    unrealized appreciation was $4,830,499,337 and gross unrealized
    depreciation was $2,566,609,090, resulting in net unrealized
    appreciation of $2,263,890,247.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    In accordance with the Trust&#160;Agreement, the Trustee
    maintains the Trust&#146;s accounting records, acts as custodian
    and transfer agent to the Trust, and provides administrative
    services, including filing of certain regulatory reports. The
    Trustee is also responsible for determining the composition of
    the portfolio of securities which must be delivered
    <FONT style="white-space: nowrap">and/or</FONT>
    received in exchange for the issuance
    <FONT style="white-space: nowrap">and/or</FONT>
    redemption of Creation Units of the Trust, and for adjusting the
    composition of the Trust&#146;s portfolio from time to time to
    conform to changes in the composition
    <FONT style="white-space: nowrap">and/or</FONT>
    weighting structure of the S&#038;P 500 Index. For these
    services, the Trustee received a fee at the following annual
    rates for the six months ended March&#160;31, 2011:
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">

</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    The Adjustment Amount is the sum of (a)&#160;the excess or
    deficiency of transaction fees received by the Trustee, less the
    expenses incurred in processing orders for creation and
    redemption of Units and (b)&#160;the amounts earned by the
    Trustee with respect to the cash held by the Trustee for the
    benefit of the Trust. During the six months ended March&#160;31,
    2011, the Adjustment Amount reduced the Trustee&#146;s fee by
    $2,119,030. The Adjustment Amount included an excess of net
    transaction fees from processing orders of $1,870,013 and a
    Trustee earnings credit of $249,017. Prior to 2008, the Trustee
    earnings credit was presented separately on the Statement of
    Operations.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt; font-size: 1pt">&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    The Trustee voluntarily agreed to waive a portion of its fee, as
    needed, for one year through February&#160;1, 2012, so that the
    total operating expenses would not exceed 9.45/100 of 1%
    (0.0945%) per annum of the daily net asset value. The total
    amount of such waivers by the Trustee for the years ended
    September&#160;30, 2008, September&#160;30, 2009,
    September&#160;30, 2010 and the six months ended March&#160;31,
    2011 was $6,923,474, $7,102,147, $10,128,612 and $6,741,256,
    respectively. The Trustee has not entered into an agreement with
    the Trust to recapture waived fees in subsequent periods and the
    Trustee may discontinue the voluntary waiver.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="margin-left: 0%; margin-right: 0%; text-indent: 0%; font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    Units are issued and redeemed by the Trust only in Creation Unit
    size aggregations of 50,000 Units. Such transactions are only
    permitted on an in-kind basis, with a separate cash payment
    which is equivalent to the undistributed net investment income
    per Unit (income equalization) and a balancing cash component to
    equate the transaction to the net asset value per unit of the
    Trust on the transaction date. A transaction fee of $3,000 is
    charged in connection with each creation or redemption of
    Creation Units through the clearing process per participating
    party per day, regardless of the number of Creation Units
    created or redeemed. In the case of redemptions outside the
    clearing process, the Transaction Fee plus an additional amount
    not to exceed three (3)&#160;times the Transaction Fee
    applicable for one Creation Unit per Creation Unit redeemed, and
    such amount is deducted from the amount delivered to the
    redeemer. Transaction fees are received by the Trustee and used
    to defray the expense of processing orders.
</DIV>
